Climate change is altering the natural pattern of the rainfall period, causing an extension of the short rains, which has begat floods,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> and reducing the drought cycle from every ten years to annual events, producing strong droughts such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008-09_Kenya_Drought" title="2008-09 Kenya Drought">2008-09 Kenya Drought</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>The temperature remains high throughout these months of tropical rain. The hottest period is February and March, leading into the season of the long rains, and the coldest is in July, until mid-August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Kenya" title="Climate change in Kenya">Climate change in Kenya</a> is increasingly impacting the lives of Kenya's citizens and the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-119">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate Change</a> has led to more frequent <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events like droughts which last longer than usual, irregular and unpredictable rainfall, flooding and increasing temperatures. The effects of these climatic changes have made already existing challenges with <a href="/wiki/Water_security" title="Water security">water security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>  and economic growth even more difficult. Harvests and agricultural production which account for about 33%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> of total <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross Domestic Product (GDP)</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF-121">[121]</a></sup> are also at risk. The increased temperatures, <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rainfall</a> variability in <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> areas, and strong <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">winds</a> associated with tropical <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a> have combined to create favorable conditions for the breeding and <a href="/wiki/Migration_(ecology)" title="Migration (ecology)">migration</a> of pests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_Salih_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_Salih-122">[122]</a></sup> An increase in temperature of up to 2.5 °C by 2050 is predicted to increase the frequency of extreme events such as <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
Hot and dry conditions in <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">Arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-Arid</a> Lands (ASALs) make <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flooding" title="Flooding">flooding</a> brought on by extreme <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> changes even more dangerous. Coastal communities are already experiencing <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> and associated challenges such as <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_intrusion" title="Saltwater intrusion">saltwater intrusion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_ReliefWeb-119">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a> and other lakes have significantly increased in size between 2010-2020<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> flooding lakeside communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup>  All these factors impact at-risk populations like marginalized communities, women and the youth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kenya_UNICEF-121">[121]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kenya" title="Wildlife of Kenya">Wildlife of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Kenya" title="Environmental issues in Kenya">Environmental issues in Kenya</a></div>
<p>Kenya has considerable land area devoted to <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> habitats, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masai_Mara" title="Masai Mara">Masai Mara</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Wildebeest" title="Blue Wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovid" title="Bovid">bovids</a> participate in a large-scale <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/migration" title="wikt:migration">annual migration</a>. More than one million wildebeest and 200,000 zebras participate in the migration across the <a href="/wiki/Mara_River" title="Mara River">Mara River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Five_Game" title="Big Five Game">"Big Five"</a> game animals of Africa, that is the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_elephant" title="African elephant">elephant</a>, can be found in Kenya and in the Masai Mara in particular. A significant population of other wild animals, reptiles, and birds can be found in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">national parks</a> and game reserves in the country. The annual animal migration occurs between June and September, with millions of animals taking part, attracting valuable foreign tourism. Two million wildebeest migrate a distance of 2,900 kilometres (1,802 mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Serengeti" title="Serengeti">Serengeti</a> in neighbouring Tanzania to the Masai Mara<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> in Kenya, in a constant clockwise fashion, searching for food and water supplies. This Serengeti Migration of the wildebeest is listed among the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Natural_Wonders_of_Africa" title="Seven Natural Wonders of Africa">Seven Natural Wonders of Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.2/10, ranking it 133rd globally out of 172 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kenya" title="Politics of Kenya">Politics of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="175" data-file-width="150" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Mwai_Kibaki%2C_October_2003.jpg" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya's third president, <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kenya is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic with a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The president is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Kenya" title="National Assembly of Kenya">National Assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Kenya" title="Senate of Kenya">Senate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. There has been growing concern, especially during former president Daniel arap Moi's tenure, that the executive was increasingly meddling with the affairs of the judiciary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya has high levels of corruption according to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> (CPI), a metric which attempts to gauge the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public-sector</a> corruption in various countries. In 2019, the nation placed 137th out of 180 countries in the index, with a score of 28 out of 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> But there are several rather significant developments with regard to curbing corruption from the Kenyan government, for instance the establishment of a new and independent <a href="/wiki/Ethics_and_Anti-Corruption_Commission" title="Ethics and Anti-Corruption Commission">Ethics and Anti-Corruption Commission (EACC)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3672" data-file-width="4896" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/220px-JUDICIARY.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/330px-JUDICIARY.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/440px-JUDICIARY.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Kenya" title="Supreme Court of Kenya">Supreme Court of Kenya</a> building.</div></div></div>
<p>Following general elections held in 1997, the Constitution of Kenya Review Act, designed to pave the way for more comprehensive amendments to the Kenyan constitution, was passed by the national parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2002, Kenya held democratic and open elections, which were judged free and fair by most international observers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The 2002 elections marked an important turning point in Kenya's democratic evolution in that power was transferred peacefully from the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_African_National_Union" title="Kenya African National Union">Kenya African National Union</a> (KANU), which had ruled the country since independence, to the <a href="/wiki/National_Rainbow_Coalition" title="National Rainbow Coalition">National Rainbow Coalition</a> (NARC), a coalition of political parties.
</p><p>Under the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>, the new ruling coalition promised to focus its efforts on generating economic growth, combating corruption, improving education, and rewriting its constitution. A few of these promises have been met. There is free primary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 2007, the government issued a statement declaring that from 2008, secondary education would be heavily subsidised, with the government footing all tuition fees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_elections_and_new_government">2013 elections and new government</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_general_election,_2013" title="Kenyan general election, 2013">Kenyan general election, 2013</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_local_elections,_2013" title="Kenyan local elections, 2013">Kenyan local elections, 2013</a></div>
<p>Under the new constitution and with President Kibaki prohibited by term limits from running for a third term, Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> ran for office. He won with 50.51% of the vote in March 2013.
</p><p>In December 2014, President Kenyatta signed a Security Laws Amendment Bill, which supporters of the law suggested was necessary to guard against armed groups. Opposition politicians, human rights groups, and nine Western countries criticised the security bill, arguing that it infringed on democratic freedoms. The governments of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> also collectively issued a press statement cautioning about the law's potential impact. Through the Jubilee Coalition, the Bill was later passed on 19 December in the National Assembly under acrimonious circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kenya" title="Foreign relations of Kenya">Foreign relations of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="980" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/220px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/330px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/440px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Nairobi, July 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya has close ties with its fellow <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>-speaking neighbours in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region. Relations with Uganda and Tanzania are generally strong, as the three nations work toward economic and social integration through common membership in the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>.
</p><p>Relations with Somalia have historically been tense, although there has been some military co-ordination against Islamist insurgents. Kenya has good relations with the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upenn_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-upenn-137">[137]</a></sup> Kenya is one of the most pro-American nations in Africa, and the wider world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>With <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> trial dates scheduled in 2013 for both President Kenyatta and Deputy President <a href="/wiki/William_Ruto" title="William Ruto">William Ruto</a> related to the 2007 election aftermath, US president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> chose not to visit the country during his <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_visits_to_Sub-Saharan_Africa#List_of_trips" title="United States presidential visits to Sub-Saharan Africa">mid-2013 African trip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Later in the summer, Kenyatta visited China at the invitation of President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> after a stop in Russia and not having visited the United States as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp01_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-140">[140]</a></sup> In July 2015, Obama visited Kenya, the first American president to visit the country while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Army_Training_Unit_Kenya" title="British Army Training Unit Kenya">British Army Training Unit Kenya</a> (BATUK) is used for the training of <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British</a> infantry battalions in the arid and rugged terrain of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Defence_Forces" title="Kenya Defence Forces">Kenya Defence Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg"><img alt="Emblem of the Kenya Defence Forces" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="326" data-file-width="385" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg/220px-Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg/330px-Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg/440px-Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Kenya_Defence_Forces.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emblem of the Kenya Defence Forces</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Kenya Defence Forces</b> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> of Kenya. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Army" title="Kenya Army">Kenya Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Navy" title="Kenya Navy">Kenya Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Air_Force" title="Kenya Air Force">Kenya Air Force</a> compose the National Defence Forces. The current Kenya Defence Forces were established, and its composition laid out, in Article 241 of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya" title="Constitution of Kenya">Constitution of Kenya</a>; the KDF is governed by the Kenya Defence Forces Act of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kenya" title="President of Kenya">President of Kenya</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of all the armed forces.
</p><p>The armed forces are regularly deployed in peacekeeping missions around the world. Further, in the aftermath of the national elections of December 2007 and the violence that subsequently engulfed the country, a commission of inquiry, the <a href="/wiki/Waki_Commission" title="Waki Commission">Waki Commission</a>, commended its readiness and adjudged it to "have performed its duty well."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Nevertheless, there have been serious allegations of human rights violations, most recently while conducting counter-insurgency operations in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt_Elgon" title="Mt Elgon">Mt Elgon</a> area<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> and also in the district of <a href="/wiki/Mandera" title="Mandera">Mandera</a> central.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya's armed forces, like many government institutions in the country, have been tainted by <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Kenya" title="Corruption in Kenya">corruption</a> allegations. Because the operations of the armed forces have been traditionally cloaked by the ubiquitous blanket of "state security", the corruption has been hidden from public view, and thus less subject to public scrutiny and notoriety. This has changed recently. In what are by Kenyan standards unprecedented revelations, in 2010, credible claims of corruption were made with regard to recruitment<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> and procurement of armoured personnel carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Further, the wisdom and prudence of certain decisions of procurement have been publicly questioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">Counties of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Divisions_of_Kenya" title="Divisions of Kenya">Divisions of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="620" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/220px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/330px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/440px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 counties</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya is divided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 semi-autonomous counties</a> that are headed by governors. These 47 counties form the first-order divisions of Kenya.
</p><p>The smallest administrative units in Kenya are called <a href="/wiki/Locations_of_Kenya" title="Locations of Kenya">locations</a>. Locations often coincide with electoral wards. Locations are usually named after their central villages/towns. Many larger towns consist of several locations. Each location has a chief, appointed by the state.
</p><p>Constituencies are an electoral subdivision, with each county comprising a whole number of constituencies. An interim boundaries commission was formed in 2010 to review the constituencies and in its report, it recommended the creation of an additional 80 constituencies. Previous to the 2013 elections, there were 210 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Kenya" title="Constituencies of Kenya">constituencies in Kenya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kenya" title="Human rights in Kenya">Human rights in Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kenya" title="LGBT rights in Kenya">LGBT rights in Kenya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Kenya" title="Human trafficking in Kenya">Human trafficking in Kenya</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexual acts</a> are illegal in Kenya and punishable by up to 14 years in prison, though the state often turns a blind eye to prosecuting gay people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> According to a 2020 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 83% of Kenyans believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewresearch.org_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-pewresearch.org-154">[154]</a></sup> While addressing a joint press conference together with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2015, President Kenyatta declined to assure Kenya's commitment to gay rights, saying that "the issue of gay rights is really a non-issue... But there are some things that we must admit we don't share. Our culture, our societies don't accept."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2008, <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> brought wide international attention<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> to <i>The Cry of Blood</i> report, which documents the extrajudicial killing of gangsters by the Kenyan police. In the report, the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="Kenya National Commission on Human Rights">Kenya National Commission on Human Rights</a> (KNCHR) reported these in their key finding "e)", stating that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">forced disappearances</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing" title="Extrajudicial killing">extrajudicial killings</a> appeared to be official policy sanctioned by the political leadership and the police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kenya" title="Economy of Kenya">Economy of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/290px-Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/435px-Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/580px-Kenya_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Kenya exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Macroeconomics" title="Macroeconomics">macroeconomic</a> outlook has steadily posted robust growth over the past few decades mostly from <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">air</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_transport" title="Water transport">water transport</a> infrastructure projects. However, much of this growth has come from cash flows diverted from ordinary Kenyan pockets at the <a href="/wiki/Microeconomics" title="Microeconomics">microeconomic</a> level through targeted <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_policy" title="Fiscal policy">fiscal</a> measures coupled with poor management, <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, massive theft of public funds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_and_the_law" title="Freedom and the law">overlegislation</a> and an ineffective <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> resulting in diminished incomes in ordinary households and <a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small businesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underemployment" title="Underemployment">underemployment</a> and general discontent across multiple sectors. Kenya ranks poorly on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Fragile_States_Index" title="List of countries by Fragile States Index">Fragile States Index</a> at number 25 out of 178 countries, ranked in 2019, and is placed in the ALERT category. In 2014, the country's macroeconomic indicators were re-based, causing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> to shift upwards to low-middle-income country status.
</p><p>Despite government assurances to the contrary, the Kenyan government is currently broke and struggling to meet its financial obligations. Junior government employees at both national and county levels are the hardest hit and have not received their monthly salaries, benefits and deductions for up to six months or more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> There is conflicting data on the state of the economy from different government agencies with official data not reflecting record inflation and very high prices of food and other basic commodities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya has a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) of 0.555 (medium), ranked 145 out of 186 in the world. As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 17.7% of Kenyans lived on less than $1.25 a day. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005-163">[163]</a></sup> In 2017, Kenya ranked 92nd in the World Bank <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business</a> rating from 113rd in 2016 (of 190 countries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The important agricultural sector is one of the least developed and largely inefficient, employing 75% of the workforce compared to less than 3% in the <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food secure</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a>.  Kenya is usually classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontier_market" title="Frontier market">frontier market</a> or occasionally an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_market" title="Emerging market">emerging market</a>, but it is not one of the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a>.
</p><p>The economy has seen much expansion, seen by strong performance in tourism, higher education, and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Kenya" title="Telecommunications in Kenya">telecommunications</a>, and decent post-drought results in agriculture, especially the vital tea sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-165">[165]</a></sup> Kenya's economy grew by more than 7% in 2007, and its foreign debt was greatly reduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-165">[165]</a></sup> This changed immediately after the disputed presidential election of December 2007, following the chaos which engulfed the country.
</p><p>Telecommunications and financial activity over the last decade now comprise 62% of GDP. 22% of GDP still comes from the unreliable agricultural sector which employs 75% of the labour force (a consistent characteristic of under-developed economies that have not attained <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>—an important catalyst of economic growth). A small portion of the population relies on food aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-166">[166]</a></sup> Industry and manufacturing is the smallest sector, accounting for 16% of GDP.  The service, industry and manufacturing sectors only employ 25% of the labour force but contribute 75% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_165-2"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-165">[165]</a></sup>
Kenya also exports textiles worth over $400 million under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AGOA" title="AGOA">AGOA</a>.
</p><p>Privatisation of state corporations like the defunct Kenya Post and Telecommunications Company, which resulted in East Africa's most profitable company—<a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Safaricom</a>, has led to their revival because of massive private investment.
</p><p>As of May 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, economic prospects are positive with 4–5% GDP growth expected, largely because of expansions in <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, transport, construction, and a recovery in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimated growth of 4.3% in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldBanki_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBanki-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="606" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png/350px-Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png/525px-Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Human_Development_Index_computed_by_the_UN.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya, Trends in the Human Development Index 1970–2010.</div></div></div>
<p>In March 1996, the presidents of Kenya, Tanzania, and Uganda re-established the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC). The EAC's objectives include harmonising tariffs and customs regimes, free movement of people, and improving regional infrastructures. In March 2004, the three East African countries signed a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">Customs Union Agreement</a>.
</p><p>Kenya has a more developed financial services sector than its neighbours. The <a href="/wiki/Nairobi_Securities_Exchange" title="Nairobi Securities Exchange">Nairobi Securities Exchange</a> (NSE) is ranked 4th in Africa in terms of market capitalisation. The Kenyan banking system is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Kenya" title="Central Bank of Kenya">Central Bank of Kenya</a> (CBK). As of late July 2004, the system consisted of 43 commercial banks (down from 48 in 2001) and several <a href="/wiki/Non-bank_financial_institution" title="Non-bank financial institution">non-bank financial institutions</a> including mortgage companies, four savings and loan associations, and several core foreign-exchange bureaus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_165-3"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/220px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/330px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/440px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amboseli_National_Park" title="Amboseli National Park">Amboseli National Park</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2433" data-file-width="6986" decoding="async" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/220px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/330px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/440px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tsavo_East_National_Park" title="Tsavo East National Park">Tsavo East National Park</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a> is the second-largest source of foreign exchange revenue following agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>  The Kenya Tourism Board is responsible for maintaining information pertaining to tourism in Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>
The main tourist attractions are photo safaris through the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">60 national parks</a> and game reserves. Other attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Wildebeest" title="Wildebeest">wildebeest</a> migration at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masaai_Mara" title="Masaai Mara">Masaai Mara</a>, which is considered to be the 7th wonder of the world; historical mosques, and colonial-era forts at <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a>; renowned scenery such as the white-capped <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kenya" title="Mount Kenya">Mount Kenya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley,_Kenya" title="Great Rift Valley, Kenya">Great Rift Valley</a>; tea plantations at <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>; coffee plantations at <a href="/wiki/Thika" title="Thika">Thika</a>; a splendid view of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a> across the border into Tanzania;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and the beaches along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" title="Swahili Coast">Swahili Coast</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Tourists, the largest number being from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, are attracted mainly to the coastal beaches and the <a href="/wiki/Game_reserve" title="Game reserve">game reserves</a>, notably, the expansive <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_East_National_Park" title="Tsavo East National Park">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_West_National_Park" title="Tsavo West National Park">Tsavo West National Park</a>, 20,808 square kilometres (8,034 sq mi) to the southeast.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kenya" title="Agriculture in Kenya">Agriculture in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2794" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/220px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/330px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/440px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tea farm near <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kericho_County" title="Kericho County">Kericho County</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Agriculture is the second largest contributor to Kenya's gross domestic product (GDP) after the service sector. In 2005, agriculture, including <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and fishing, accounted for 24% of GDP, as well as for 18% of wage employment and 50% of revenue from exports. The principal <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crops</a> are tea, horticultural produce, and coffee. Horticultural produce and tea are the main growth sectors and the two most valuable of all of Kenya's exports. The production of major food staples such as <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> is subject to sharp weather-related fluctuations. Production downturns periodically necessitate food aid—for example in 2004, due to one of Kenya's intermittent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Droughts" title="Droughts">droughts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>A consortium led by the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICRISAT" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) has had some success in helping farmers grow new <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon pea</a> varieties instead of maize, in particularly dry areas. Pigeon peas are very drought-resistant, so can be grown in areas with less than 650 millimetres (26 in) annual rainfall. Successive projects encouraged the commercialisation of legumes by stimulating the growth of local seed production and agro-dealer networks for distribution and marketing. This work, which included linking producers to wholesalers, helped to increase local producer prices by 20–25% in Nairobi and Mombasa. The commercialisation of the pigeon pea is now enabling some farmers to buy assets ranging from mobile phones to productive land and livestock, and is opening pathways for them to move out of poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tea, coffee, sisal, pyrethrum, corn, and wheat are grown in the fertile highlands, one of the most successful agricultural production regions in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-115">[115]</a></sup> Livestock predominates in the semi-arid savanna to the north and east. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconuts" title="Coconuts">Coconuts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pineapples" title="Pineapples">pineapples</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cashew_nuts" title="Cashew nuts">cashew nuts</a>, cotton, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, and corn are grown in the lower-lying areas. Kenya has not attained the level of investment and efficiency in agriculture that can guarantee food security, and coupled with resulting poverty (53% of the population lives below the poverty line), a significant portion of the population regularly starves and is heavily dependent on food aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-166">[166]</a></sup> Poor roads, an inadequate railway network, under-used water transport, and expensive air transport have isolated mostly <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a> areas, and farmers in other regions often leave food to rot in the fields because they cannot access markets. This was last seen in August and September 2011, prompting the <a href="/wiki/Kenyans_for_Kenya" title="Kenyans for Kenya">Kenyans for Kenya</a> initiative by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/220px-Kapsowar1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/330px-Kapsowar1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/440px-Kapsowar1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agricultural countryside in Kenya</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> sector is categorised into three organizational types: <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholder</a> schemes, centrally-managed public schemes, and private/commercial irrigation schemes.
</p><p>The smallholder schemes are owned, developed, and managed by individuals or groups of farmers operating as water users or self-help groups. Irrigation is carried out on individual or on group farms averaging 0.1–0.4 ha. There are about 3,000 smallholder irrigation schemes covering a total area of 47,000 ha.
The country has seven large, centrally managed irrigation schemes, namely Mwea, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bura_irrigation_and_Settlement_Project_(Kenya)" title="Bura irrigation and Settlement Project (Kenya)">Bura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hola,_Kenya" title="Hola, Kenya">Hola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perkerra_River" title="Perkerra River">Perkera</a>, West Kano, Bunyala, and <a href="/wiki/Ahero" title="Ahero">Ahero</a>, covering a total area of 18,200 ha and averaging 2,600 ha per scheme. These schemes are managed by the National Irrigation Board and account for 18% of irrigated land area in Kenya.
Large-scale private commercial farms cover 45,000 hectares, accounting for 40% of irrigated land. They utilise high technology and produce high-value crops for the export market, especially flowers and vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya is the world's 3rd largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cut_flowers" title="Cut flowers">cut flowers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-175">[175]</a></sup> Roughly half of Kenya's 127 flower farms are concentrated around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Naivasha" title="Lake Naivasha">Lake Naivasha</a>, 90 kilometres northwest of Nairobi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-175">[175]</a></sup> To speed their export, Nairobi airport has a terminal dedicated to the transport of flowers and vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_manufacturing">Industry and manufacturing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2269" data-file-width="6152" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/300px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/450px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/600px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenya_Commercial_Bank" title="Kenya Commercial Bank">Kenya Commercial Bank</a> office at KENCOM House (right) in Nairobi.</div></div></div>
<p>Although Kenya is a low middle-income country, manufacturing accounts for 14% of the GDP, with industrial activity concentrated around the three largest urban centres of <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kisumu" title="Kisumu">Kisumu</a>, and is dominated by food-processing industries such as grain milling, beer production, sugarcane crushing, and the fabrication of consumer goods, e.g., vehicles from kits.
</p><p>Kenya also has a cement production industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Kenya has an <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a> that processes imported crude petroleum into petroleum products, mainly for the domestic market. In addition, a substantial and expanding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a> commonly referred to as <i>jua kali</i> engages in small-scale manufacturing of household goods, auto parts, and farm implements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya's inclusion among the beneficiaries of the US Government's African Growth and Opportunity Act (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AGOA" title="AGOA">AGOA</a>) has given a boost to manufacturing in recent years. Since AGOA took effect in 2000, Kenya's clothing sales to the United States increased from US$44 million to US$270 million (2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Other initiatives to strengthen manufacturing have been the new government's favourable tax measures, including the removal of duty on capital equipment and other raw materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kenya" title="Transport in Kenya">Transport in Kenya</a></div>
<p>The country has an extensive network of paved and unpaved roads. Kenya's railway system links the nation's ports and major cities, connecting it with neighbouring Uganda. There are 15 airports which have paved runways.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya" title="Energy in Kenya">Energy in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/170px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/255px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/340px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Workers at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria_II_Geothermal_Power_Station" title="Olkaria II Geothermal Power Station">Olkaria Geothermal Power Plant</a></div></div></div>
<p>The largest share of Kenya's electricity supply comes from geothermal energy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> followed by hydroelectric stations at dams along the upper <a href="/wiki/Tana_River_(Kenya)" title="Tana River (Kenya)">Tana River</a>, as well as the Turkwel Gorge Dam in the west. A petroleum-fired plant on the coast, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power_in_Kenya" title="Geothermal power in Kenya">geothermal facilities</a> at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria" title="Olkaria">Olkaria</a> (near Nairobi), and electricity imported from <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> make up the rest of the supply. A <a href="/wiki/Sodo%E2%80%93Moyale%E2%80%93Suswa_High_Voltage_Power_Line" title="Sodo–Moyale–Suswa High Voltage Power Line">2,000 MW powerline from Ethiopia</a> is nearing completion.
</p><p>Kenya's installed capacity increased from 1,142 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatts" title="Megawatts">megawatts</a> between 2001 and 2003 to 2,341 in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Electricity_Generating_Company" title="Kenya Electricity Generating Company">Kenya Electricity Generating Company (KenGen)</a>, established in 1997 under the name of Kenya Power Company, handles the generation of electricity, while Kenya Power handles the electricity transmission and distribution system in the country. Shortfalls of electricity occur periodically, when drought reduces water flow. To become energy sufficient, Kenya has installed <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Kenya" title="Wind power in Kenya">wind power</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Kenya" title="Solar power in Kenya">solar power</a> (over 300 MW each), and aims to build a nuclear power plant by 2027.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya has proven deposits of oil in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a> estimates the country's oil reserves to be around one billion barrels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Exploration is still continuing to determine whether there are more reserves. Kenya currently imports all crude petroleum requirements. It has no strategic reserves and relies solely on oil marketers' 21-day oil reserves required under industry regulations. Petroleum accounts for 20% to 25% of the national import bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_investment_and_trade">Chinese investment and trade</span></h3>
<p>Published comments on Kenya's <a href="/wiki/98.4_Capital_FM" title="98.4 Capital FM">Capital FM</a> website by Liu Guangyuan, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Ambassador_to_Kenya" title="Chinese Ambassador to Kenya">China's ambassador to Kenya</a>, at the time of President Kenyatta's 2013 trip to Beijing, said, "Chinese investment in Kenya ... reached $474 million, representing Kenya's largest source of foreign direct investment, and ... bilateral trade ... reached $2.84 billion" in 2012. Kenyatta was "[a]ccompanied by 60 Kenyan business people [and hoped to] ... gain support from China for a planned $2.5 billion railway from the southern Kenyan port of Mombasa to neighbouring Uganda, as well as a nearly $1.8 billion dam", according to a statement from the president's office, also at the time of the trip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp01_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Base Titanium, a subsidiary of Base resources of Australia, shipped its first major consignment of minerals to China. About 25,000 tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Ilmenite" title="Ilmenite">ilmenite</a> was flagged off the Kenyan coastal town of Kilifi. The first shipment was expected to earn Kenya about KSh.15–20 billion/= in earnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> In 2014, the Chinese contracted railway project from Nairobi to Mombasa was suspended due to a dispute over compensation for land acquisition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vision_2030">Vision 2030</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="663" data-file-width="1525" decoding="async" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/220px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/330px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/440px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The official logo of <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, the Kenyan government unveiled <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>, an economic development programme it hopes will put the country in the same league as the <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian Economic Tigers</a> by 2030. In 2013, it launched a National Climate Change Action Plan, having acknowledged that omitting climate as a key development issue in Vision 2030 was an oversight failure. The 200-page Action Plan, developed with support from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a>, sets out the Government of Kenya's vision for a 'low-carbon climate resilient development pathway'. At the launch in March 2013, the Secretary of the Ministry of Planning, National Development, and Vision 2030 emphasized that climate would be a central issue in the renewed Medium-Term Plan that would be launched in the coming months. This would create a direct and robust delivery framework for the Action Plan and ensure climate change is treated as an economy-wide issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Furthermore, Kenya submitted an updated, more ambitious NDC on December 24, 2020, with a commitment to abate greenhouse gases by 32 percent by 2030 relative to the business-as-usual scenario and in line with its sustainable development agenda and national circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_exploration">Oil exploration</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya#Petroleum" title="Energy in Kenya">Oil in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2825" data-file-width="4253" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/220px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/330px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/440px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a> borders Turkana County</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya has proven oil deposits in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana County</a>. President Mwai Kibaki announced on 26 March 2012 that <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a>, an Anglo-Irish oil exploration firm, had struck oil, but its commercial viability and subsequent production would take about three years to confirm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early in 2006, Chinese president <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> signed an oil exploration contract with Kenya, part of a series of deals designed to keep Africa's natural resources flowing to China's rapidly expanding economy.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/220px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/330px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg/440px-Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lions_Family_Portrait_Masai_Mara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A family of lions in <a href="/wiki/Maasai_Mara" title="Maasai Mara">Maasai Mara</a></div></div></div>
<p>The deal allowed for China's state-controlled offshore oil and gas company, <a href="/wiki/China_National_Offshore_Oil_Corporation" title="China National Offshore Oil Corporation">CNOOC</a>, to prospect for oil in Kenya, which is just beginning to drill its first exploratory wells on the borders of Sudan and the disputed area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a>, on the border with <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and in coastal waters. There are formal estimates of the possible reserves of oil discovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_labour_and_prostitution">Child labour and prostitution</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="855" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/220px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/330px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/440px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai people</a>. The Maasai live in both Kenya and Tanzania.</div></div></div>
<p>Child labour <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_labor_in_Kenya" title="Child labor in Kenya">is common in Kenya</a>. Most working children are active in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-193">[193]</a></sup> In 2006, UNICEF estimated that up to 30% of girls in the coastal areas of Malindi, Mombasa, Kilifi, and Diani were subject to prostitution. Most of the prostitutes in Kenya are aged 9–18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-193">[193]</a></sup> The Ministry of Gender and Child Affairs employed 400 child protection officers in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_193-2"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-193">[193]</a></sup> The causes of child labour include poverty, the lack of access to education, and weak government institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya_193-3"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_–_Kenya-193">[193]</a></sup> Kenya has ratified Convention No. 81 on labour inspection in industries and Convention No. 129 on labour inspection in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/220px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/330px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/440px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Child labour in Kenya</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Microfinance">Microfinance</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microfinance_in_Kenya" title="Microfinance in Kenya">Microfinance in Kenya</a></div>
<p>More than 20 institutions offer business loans on a large scale, specific agriculture loans, education loans, and loans for other purposes. Additionally, there are:
</p>
<ul><li>emergency loans, which are more expensive in respect to interest rates, but are quickly available</li>
<li>group loans for smaller groups (four to five members) and larger groups (up to 30 members)</li>
<li>women's loans, which are also available to groups of women</li></ul>
<p>Out of approximately 40 million Kenyans, about 14 million are unable to receive financial service through formal loan application services, and an additional 12 million have no access to financial service institutions at all. Further, one million Kenyans are reliant on informal groups for receiving financial aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Conditions for microfinance products</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Eligibility criteria: the general criteria might include gender as in the case of special women's loans; being at least 18 years old; owning a valid Kenyan ID; having a business; demonstrating the ability to repay the loan; and being a customer of the institution.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Credit_scoring" title="Credit scoring">Credit scoring</a>: there is no advanced credit scoring system and the majority has not stated any official loan distribution system. However, some institutions require applicants to have an existing business for at least three months, own a small amount of cash, provide the institution with a business plan or proposal, have at least one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarantor" title="Guarantor">guarantor</a>, or to attend group meetings or training. For group loans, almost half of the institutions require group members to guarantee for each other.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">Interest rate</a>: mostly calculated on a flat basis and some at a declining balance. More than 90% of the institutions require monthly interest payments. The average interest rate is 30–40% for loans up to KSh.500,000/=. For loans above KSh.500,000/=, interest rates go up to 71%.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kenya" title="Demographics of Kenya">Demographics of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/170px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/255px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/340px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> woman in traditional attire</div></div></div>
