<p>Kenya had a population of approximately 48 million in January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia-11">[11]</a></sup> The country has a young population, with 73% of residents under 30 because of rapid <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> from 2.9 million to 40 million inhabitants over the last century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nairobi is home to <a href="/wiki/Kibera" title="Kibera">Kibera</a>, one of the world's largest slums. The shantytown is believed to house between 170,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nation1_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-nation1-201">[201]</a></sup> and one million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The UNHCR base in <a href="/wiki/Dadaab" title="Dadaab">Dadaab</a> in the north houses around 500,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DadaabPop_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-DadaabPop-203">[203]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>
<p>Kenya has a diverse population that includes many of Africa's major ethnoracial and linguistic groups. Although there is no official list of Kenyan ethnic groups, the number of ethnic categories and sub-categories recorded in the country's census has changed significantly over time, expanding from 42 in 1969 to more than 120 in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balaton-Chrimes2020_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balaton-Chrimes2020-204">[204]</a></sup> Most residents are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantus</a> (60%) or <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotes</a> (30%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-205">[205]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> groups also form a small ethnic minority, as do Arabs, Indians, and Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okothndaloh_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Okothndaloh-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Kenya National Bureau of Statistics">Kenya National Bureau of Statistics</a> (KNBS), in 2019, Kenya had a total population of 47,564,296. The largest native ethnic groups were the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> (8,148,668), <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> (6,823,842), <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a> (6,358,113), <a href="/wiki/Luo_people" title="Luo people">Luo</a> (5,066,966), <a href="/wiki/Kamba_people" title="Kamba people">Kamba</a> (4,663,910), <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a> (2,780,502), <a href="/wiki/Kisii_people" title="Kisii people">Kisii</a> (2,703,235), <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a> (2,488,691), <a href="/wiki/Meru_people" title="Meru people">Meru</a> (1,975,869), <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> (1,189,522), and <a href="/wiki/Turkana_people" title="Turkana people">Turkana</a> (1,016,174). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a> of Kenya, formerly known as NFD, is predominantly inhabited by the indigenous ethnic <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a>. Foreign-rooted populations include <a href="/wiki/Omanis" title="Omanis">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Kenya" title="Indians in Kenya">Asians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_people_in_Kenya" title="White people in Kenya">Europeans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kenya" title="Languages of Kenya">Languages of Kenya</a></div>
<p>Kenya's various ethnic groups typically speak their mother tongues within their own communities. The two <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>, English and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, are used in varying degrees of fluency for communication with other populations. English is widely spoken in commerce, schooling, and government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cugrwed_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cugrwed-207">[207]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peri-urbanisation" title="Peri-urbanisation">Peri-urban</a> and rural dwellers are less multilingual, with many in rural areas speaking only their native languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broassim_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broassim-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> is primarily used in Kenya. Additionally, a distinct local dialect, <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_English" title="Kenyan English">Kenyan English</a>, is used by some communities and individuals in the country, and contains features unique to it that were derived from local <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a> such as Kiswahili and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gikuyu_language" title="Gikuyu language">Kikuyu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cliike_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cliike-209">[209]</a></sup> It has been developing since colonisation and also contains certain elements of <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sheng_slang" title="Sheng slang">Sheng</a> is a Kiswahili-based <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">cant</a> spoken in some urban areas. Primarily a mixture of Swahili and English, it is an example of linguistic <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">code-switching</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nphil_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nphil-210">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>69 languages are spoken in Kenya. Most belong to two broad language families: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niger-Congo_languages" title="Niger-Congo languages">Niger-Congo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu branch</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">Nilotic branch</a>), spoken by the country's Bantu and Nilotic populations respectively. The Cushitic and Arab ethnic minorities speak languages belonging to the separate <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family, with the Indian and European residents speaking languages from the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnken_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnken-211">[211]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kenya" title="Religion in Kenya">Religion in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/220px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/330px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/440px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Holy Ghost Roman Catholic Cathedral in Mombasa.</div></div></div>
<p>Most Kenyans are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> (85.5%), with 53.9% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> and 20.6% <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Kenya" title="Catholic Church in Kenya">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Presbyterian Church of East Africa">Presbyterian Church of East Africa</a> has 3 million followers in Kenya and surrounding countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> There are smaller conservative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed</a> churches, the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Evangelical_Presbyterian_Church" title="Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church">Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Presbyterian_Church_in_Kenya" title="Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya">Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Reformed Church of East Africa">Reformed Church of East Africa</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</a> has 621,200 adherents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Kenya has by far the highest number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">Quakers</a> of any country in the world, with around 146,300.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> The only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_synagogue" title="Jewish synagogue">Jewish synagogue</a> in the country is in Nairobi.
</p><p>Islam is the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kenya" title="Islam in Kenya">second largest religion</a>, comprising 10.9% of the population. 60% of Kenyan Muslims live in the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Province" title="Coast Province">Coastal Region</a>, comprising 50% of the total population there, while the upper part of Kenya's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province_(Kenya)" title="Eastern Province (Kenya)">Eastern Region</a> is home to 10% of the country's Muslims, where they are the majority religious group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" title="African traditional religion">Indigenous beliefs</a> are practised by 0.7% of the population, although many self-identifying Christians and Muslims <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">maintain some traditional beliefs and customs</a>. Nonreligious Kenyans are 1.6% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Hindus also live in Kenya. The numbers are estimated to be around 60,287, or 0.13% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2019a_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-Census2019a-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Kenya" title="Health in Kenya">Health in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/220px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/330px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/440px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outpatient Department of AIC Kapsowar Hospital<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Kapsowar" title="Kapsowar">Kapsowar</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Health care is largely funded by private individuals, families and employers through direct payments to <a href="/wiki/Health_care_provider" title="Health care provider">health care providers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hospital_Insurance_Fund" title="National Hospital Insurance Fund">National Health Insurance Fund</a>, and private health insurance firms. Additional funding comes from local, international and some government <a href="/wiki/Social_safety_net" title="Social safety net">social safety net</a> schemes. Public hospitals are <a href="/wiki/Fee-for-service" title="Fee-for-service">fee-for-service</a> establishments that generate a large portion of county and national government revenues, making them highly political enterprises. Minimum and maximum fees that health care providers may charge are determined and controlled by the government through the regulatory bodies.
</p><p>Kenya is currently grappling with a large number of unemployed health care providers (including health facilities) many of whom are under-utilised, underemployed or not practicing. A large thriving <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">black market</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counterfeit_medicines" title="Counterfeit medicines">counterfeit medicines</a> and health services exists and is largely controlled by <a href="/wiki/Quackery" title="Quackery">quacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charlatan" title="Charlatan">charlatans</a>. Kenya is a major regional transit route and destination for <a href="/wiki/Counterfeit_medications" title="Counterfeit medications">counterfeit medications</a> and other health products. The corporate practice of medicine is a deeply entrenched vice that has not been subjected to <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a> resulting in widespread sharing of medical practice incomes with non-medical persons and, more recently, in the actual trading of patients and health care providers in <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>Private health facilities are diverse, highly dynamic, and difficult to classify, unlike public health facilities, which are easily grouped in classes that consist of community-based (level I) services, run by <a href="/wiki/Community_health_worker" title="Community health worker">community health workers</a>; dispensaries (level II facilities) run by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurses</a>; health centres (level III facilities), run by <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officers</a>; sub-county hospitals (level IV facilities), which may be run by a <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officer</a> or a <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">medical officer</a>; county hospitals (level V facilities), which may be run by a <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">medical officer</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Consultant_(medicine)" title="Consultant (medicine)">medical practitioner</a>; and national referral hospitals (level VI facilities), which are run by fully qualified <a href="/wiki/Consultant_(medicine)" title="Consultant (medicine)">medical practitioners</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="323" data-file-width="1218" decoding="async" height="58" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/220px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/330px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/440px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Table showing different grades of clinical officers, medical officers, and medical practitioners in Kenya's public service</div></div></div> <p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurses" title="Nurses">Nurses</a> are by far the largest group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front-line" title="Front-line">front-line</a> health care providers in all sectors, followed by clinical officers, medical officers, and medical practitioners. These are absorbed and deployed into government service in accordance with the <b>Scheme of Service for Nursing Personnel (2014)</b>, the <b>Revised Scheme of Service for Clinical Personnel (2020)</b> and the <b>Revised Scheme of Service for Medical Officers and Dental Officers (2016)</b>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_healer" title="Traditional healer">Traditional healers</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalist" title="Herbalist">herbalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctors</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faith_healer" title="Faith healer">faith healers</a>) are readily available, trusted, and widely consulted as practitioners of first or last choice by both rural and urban dwellers.
</p><p>Despite major achievements in the health sector, Kenya still faces many challenges. The estimated <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> dropped in 2009 to approximately 55 years — five years below the 1990 level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate was high at approximately 44 deaths per 1,000 children in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> The WHO estimated in 2011 that only 42% of births were attended by a skilled health professional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Diseases_of_poverty" title="Diseases of poverty">Diseases of poverty</a> directly correlate with a country's <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic performance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wealth_distribution" title="Wealth distribution">wealth distribution</a>: Half of Kenyans live below the poverty level.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Preventable diseases like malaria, HIV/AIDS, pneumonia, diarrhoea, and malnutrition are the biggest burden, major child-killers, and responsible for much morbidity; weak policies, corruption, inadequate health workers, weak management, and poor leadership in the public health sector are largely to blame. According to 2009 estimates, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">HIV/AIDS prevalence</a> is about 6.3% of the adult population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> However, the 2011 UNAIDS Report suggests that the HIV epidemic may be improving in Kenya, as HIV prevalence is declining among young people (ages 15–24) and pregnant women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Kenya had an estimated 15 million cases of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Kenya" title="Women in Kenya">Women in Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Kenya" title="Child marriage in Kenya">Child marriage in Kenya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Kenya" title="Polygamy in Kenya">Polygamy in Kenya</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in Kenya was estimated to be 4.49 children per woman in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> According to a 2008–09 survey by the Kenyan government, the total fertility rate was 4.6% and the contraception usage rate among married women was 46%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality">Maternal mortality</a> is high, partly because of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Female_genital_cutting" title="Female genital cutting">female genital mutilation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_165-4"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-165">[165]</a></sup> with about 27% of women having undergone it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup>
This practice is however on the decline as the country becomes more modernised, and in 2011 it was banned in Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup>
Women were economically empowered before colonialisation.
By colonial land alienation, women lost access and control of land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-231">[231]</a></sup> They became more economically dependent on men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-231">[231]</a></sup> A colonial order of gender emerged where males dominated females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-231">[231]</a></sup>
Median age at first marriage increases with increasing education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup>
Rape, defilement, and battering are not always seen as serious crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-233">[233]</a></sup>
Reports of sexual assault are not always taken seriously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span></h3>
<p>Article 260 of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Kenyan_constitutional_referendum" title="2010 Kenyan constitutional referendum">Kenyan Constitution</a> of 2010 defines youth as those between the ages of 18 and 34.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> According to the 2019 Population and Census results, 75 percent of the 47.6 million population is under the age of 35, making Kenya a country of the <a href="/wiki/Youth" title="Youth">youth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Youth unemployment and underemployment in Kenya has become a problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> According to the Kenya National Bureau of Statistics (KNBS), approximately 1.7 million people lost their jobs as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic, which eliminated some informal jobs and caused the economy to slow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> The Kenyan government has made progress in addressing the high youth unemployment by implementing various affirmative action programs and projects which include; the <a href="/wiki/National_Youth_Service_(Kenya)" title="National Youth Service (Kenya)">National Youth Service</a>, The National Youth Enterprise Development Fund,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> The Women Enterprise Fund,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Kazi Mtaani, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ajira_Digital_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ajira Digital Program (page does not exist)">Ajira Digital</a>, Kikao Mtaani,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Uwezo fund,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> Future Bora<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> and Studio mashinani<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> that <a href="/wiki/Youth_empowerment" title="Youth empowerment">empower the youth</a>, offer job opportunities and to raise one's standard of living.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kenya" title="Education in Kenya">Education in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/220px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/330px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/440px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>School children in a classroom.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/220px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/330px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/440px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An MSc student at <a href="/wiki/Kenyatta_University" title="Kenyatta University">Kenyatta University</a> in Nairobi.</div></div></div>
<p>Children attend nursery school, or kindergarten in the private sector until they are five years old. This lasts one to three years (KG1, KG2 and KG3) and is financed privately because there has been no government policy on pre-schooling until recently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p><p>Basic formal education starts at age six and lasts 12 years, consisting of eight years in primary school and four in high school or secondary. Primary school is free in public schools and those attending can join a vocational youth/village polytechnic, or make their own arrangements for an apprenticeship program and learn a trade such as tailoring, carpentry, motor vehicle repair, brick-laying and masonry for about two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>Those who complete high school can join a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">polytechnic</a> or other technical college and study for three years, or proceed directly to university and study for four years. Graduates from the polytechnics and colleges can then join the workforce and later obtain a specialised higher diploma qualification after a further one to two years of training, or join the university—usually in the second or third year of their respective course. The <a href="/wiki/Higher_diploma" title="Higher diploma">higher diploma</a> is accepted by many employers in place of a bachelor's degree and direct or accelerated admission to post-graduate studies is possible in some universities.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="886" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/220px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/330px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/440px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Maasai girl at school.</div></div></div>
<p>Public universities in Kenya are highly commercialised institutions and only a small fraction of qualified high school graduates are admitted on limited government-sponsorship into programs of their choice. Most are admitted into the social sciences, which are cheap to run, or as self-sponsored students paying the full cost of their studies. Most qualified students who miss out opt for middle-level diploma programs in public or private universities, colleges, and polytechnics.
</p><p>In 2018, 18.5 percent of the Kenyan adult population was illiterate, which was the highest rate of literacy in East Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> There are very wide regional disparities: for example, Nairobi had the highest level of literacy at 87.1 per cent, compared to North Eastern Province, the lowest, at 8.0 per cent. Preschool, which targets children from age three to five, is an integral component of the education system and is a key requirement for admission to Standard One (First Grade). At the end of primary education, pupils sit the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Primary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Primary Education">Kenya Certificate of Primary Education</a> (KCPE), which determines those who proceed to secondary school or vocational training. The result of this examination is needed for placement at secondary school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>Primary school is for students aged 6/7-13/14 years. For those who proceed to the secondary level, there is a national examination at the end of Form Four – the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education">Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (KCSE), which determines those proceeding to the universities, other professional training, or employment. Students sit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Examinations" title="Examinations">examinations</a> in eight subjects of their choosing. However, English, Kiswahili, and mathematics are compulsory subjects.
</p><p>The Kenya Universities and Colleges Central Placement Service (KUCCPS), formerly the Joint Admissions Board (JAB), is responsible for selecting students joining the public universities. Other than the public schools, there are many private schools, mainly in urban areas. Similarly, there are a number of <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international schools</a> catering to various overseas educational systems.
</p><p>Despite its impressive commercial approach, Kenya's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia" title="Academia">academia</a> and higher education system is somehow rigid. However, Kenyan University Graduates are highly skilled, and they are accepted in the job market domestically as well as internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> Kenay was ranked 85th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> in 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">Culture of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1089" data-file-width="1384" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/220px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/330px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/440px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan boys and girls performing a traditional dance</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/220px-Nation_media_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/330px-Nation_media_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/440px-Nation_media_house.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nation Media House, which hosts the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">culture of Kenya</a> comprises multiple traditions. Kenya has no single prominent culture. It instead consists of the various cultures of the country's different communities.
</p><p>Notable populations include the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a> on the coast, several other <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> communities in the central and western regions, and Nilotic communities in the northwest. The <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> culture is well known to tourism, despite constituting a relatively small part of Kenya's population. They are renowned for their elaborate upper-body adornment and jewellery.
</p><p>Additionally, Kenya has an extensive music, television, and theatre scene.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_Kenya" title="Media of Kenya">Media of Kenya</a></div>
<p>Kenya has a number of media outlets that broadcast domestically and globally. They cover news, business, sports, and entertainment. Popular Kenyan newspapers include:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Nation" title="Daily Nation">The Daily Nation</a></i>; part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group (NMG)</a> (largest market share)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Standard_(Kenya)" title="The Standard (Kenya)">The Standard</a></i></li>
<li><i>The Star</i></li>
<li><i>The People</i></li>
<li><i>East Africa Weekly</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Taifa_Leo" title="Taifa Leo">Taifa Leo</a></i></li></ul>
<p>Television stations based in Kenya include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Kenya Broadcasting Corporation">Kenya Broadcasting Corporation</a> (KBC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Citizen_TV" title="Citizen TV">Citizen TV</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Television_Network" title="Kenya Television Network">Kenya Television Network</a> (KTN)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NTV_(Kenya)" title="NTV (Kenya)">NTV</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a> (NMG))</li>
<li>Kiss Television</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K24_(Kenya)" title="K24 (Kenya)">K24 Television</a></li>
<li>Kass-TV</li></ul>
<p>All these terrestrial channels are transmitted via a DVB T2 digital TV signal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_literature" title="Kenyan literature">Kenyan literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="591" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/220px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/330px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/440px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan author <a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o">Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o">Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o</a> is one of Kenya's best-known writers. His novel <i><a href="/wiki/Weep_Not,_Child" title="Weep Not, Child">Weep Not, Child</a> depicts</i> life in Kenya during the British occupation. The story details the effects of the Mau Mau on the lives of Kenyans. Its combination of themes—<a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, education, and love—helped make it one of the best-known African novels.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.G._Vassanji" title="M.G. Vassanji">M.G. Vassanji</a>'s 2003 novel <i>The In-Between World of Vikram Lall</i> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Giller_Prize" title="Scotiabank Giller Prize">Giller Prize</a> in 2003. It is the fictional memoir of a Kenyan of Indian heritage and his family as they adjust to the changing political climates in colonial and post-colonial Kenya.
</p><p>Since 2003, the literary journal <i><a href="/wiki/Kwani%3F" title="Kwani?">Kwani?</a></i> has been publishing Kenyan contemporary literature. Kenya has also nurtured emerging versatile authors such as Paul Kipchumba (Kipwendui, Kibiwott) who demonstrate a pan-African outlook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kenya" title="Music of Kenya">Music of Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juacali_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2880" data-file-width="2160" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Juacali_1.jpg/170px-Juacali_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Juacali_1.jpg/255px-Juacali_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Juacali_1.jpg/340px-Juacali_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juacali_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Popular Kenyan musician <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya has a diverse assortment of popular music forms, in addition to multiple types of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> based on the variety of over 40 regional languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>Drums are the most dominant instrument in popular Kenyan music. Drum beats are very complex and include both native rhythms and imported ones, especially the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> <a href="/wiki/Cavacha" title="Cavacha">cavacha</a> rhythm. Popular Kenyan music usually involves the interplay of multiple parts, and more recently, showy guitar solos as well. There are also a number of local hip-hop artists, including <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a>; Afro-pop bands such as <a href="/wiki/Sauti_Sol" title="Sauti Sol">Sauti Sol</a>; and musicians who play local genres like Benga, such as <a href="/wiki/Akothee" title="Akothee">Akothee</a>.
</p><p>Lyrics are most often in Kiswahili or English. There is also some emerging aspect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a> borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> musicians. Lyrics are also written in local languages. Urban radio generally only plays English music, though there also exist a number of vernacular radio stations.
</p><p>Zilizopendwa is a genre of local urban music that was recorded in the 1960s, 70s, and 80s by musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Daudi_Kabaka" title="Daudi Kabaka">Daudi Kabaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fadhili_William" title="Fadhili William">Fadhili William</a>, and Sukuma Bin Ongaro, and is particularly enjoyed by older people—having been popularised by the Kenya Broadcasting Corporation's Kiswahili service (formerly called Voice of Kenya or VOK).
</p><p>The Isukuti is a vigorous dance performed by the <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> sub-tribes to the beat of a traditional drum called the Isukuti during many occasions such as the birth of a child, marriage, or funeral. Other traditional dances include the <a href="/wiki/Ohangla" title="Ohangla">Ohangla</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Luo_peoples" title="Luo peoples">Luo</a>, Nzele among the <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mugithi" title="Mugithi">Mugithi</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">Taarab</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a>.
</p><p>Additionally, Kenya has a growing Christian gospel music scene. Prominent local gospel musicians include the <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_Boys_Choir" title="Kenyan Boys Choir">Kenyan Boys Choir</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Benga_music" title="Benga music">Benga music</a> has been popular since the late 1960s, especially in the area around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>. The word <i>benga</i> is occasionally used to refer to any kind of pop music. Bass, guitar, and percussion are the usual instruments.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kenya" title="Sport in Kenya">Sport in Kenya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/220px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/330px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/440px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jepkosgei Kipyego and Jepkemoi Cheruiyot at the 2012 London Olympics</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya is active in several sports, among them <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>. The country is known chiefly for its dominance in <a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_running" title="Middle-distance running">middle-distance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long-distance_running" title="Long-distance running">long-distance</a> athletics, having consistently produced <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> champions in various distance events, especially in 800 m, 1,500 m, 3,000 m steeplechase, 5,000 m, 10,000 m, and the marathon. Kenyan athletes (particularly <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a>), continue to dominate the world of distance running, although competition from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> has reduced this supremacy. Kenya's best-known athletes include the four-time women's <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a> winner and two-time world champion <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Ndereba" title="Catherine Ndereba">Catherine Ndereba</a>, 800m world record holder <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marathon_(sport)" title="Marathon (sport)">marathon</a> world record-holder <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">Paul Tergat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Ngugi" title="John Ngugi">John Ngugi</a>.
</p><p>Kenya won several medals during the Beijing Olympics: six gold, four silver, and four bronze, making it Africa's most successful nation in the 2008 Olympics. New athletes gained attention, such as <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Jelimo" title="Pamela Jelimo">Pamela Jelimo</a>, the women's 800m gold medalist who went on to win the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_Golden_League" title="IAAF Golden League">IAAF Golden League</a> jackpot, and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wanjiru" title="Samuel Wanjiru">Samuel Wanjiru</a>, who won the men's marathon. Retired Olympic and Commonwealth Games champion <a href="/wiki/Kipchoge_Keino" title="Kipchoge Keino">Kipchoge Keino</a> helped usher in Kenya's ongoing distance dynasty in the 1970s and was followed by Commonwealth Champion <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rono" title="Henry Rono">Henry Rono</a>'s spectacular string of world record performances. Lately, there has been controversy in Kenyan athletics circles, with the defection of a number of Kenyan athletes to represent other countries, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAAF_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-253">[253]</a></sup> The Kenyan Ministry of Sports has tried to stop the defections, but they have continued anyway, with <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lagat" title="Bernard Lagat">Bernard Lagat</a> being the latest, choosing to represent the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAAF_253-1"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-253">[253]</a></sup> Most of these defections occur because of economic or financial factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> Decisions by the Kenyan government to tax athletes' earnings may also be a motivating factor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> Some elite Kenyan runners who cannot qualify for their country's strong national team find it easier to qualify by running for other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/220px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/330px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/440px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan Olympic and world record holder in the 800 meters, <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Kenya has been a dominant force in women's volleyball within Africa, with both the clubs and the national team winning various continental championships in the past decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> The women's team has competed at the Olympics and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women's World Championship">World Championships</a>, though without any notable success. Cricket is another popular sport, also ranking as the most successful team sport. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_cricket_team" title="Kenyan cricket team">Kenya</a> has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> since <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996</a>. They upset some of the world's best teams and reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">2003 tournament</a>. They won the inaugural World Cricket League Division 1 hosted in Nairobi and participated in the World T20. They also participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_World_Cup_2011" title="ICC Cricket World Cup 2011">ICC Cricket World Cup 2011</a>. Their current captain is <a href="/wiki/Rakep_Patel" title="Rakep Patel">Rakep Patel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya is represented by <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Onyango" title="Lucas Onyango">Lucas Onyango</a> as a professional rugby league player who plays with the English club <a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham</a>. Besides the former <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> team, he has played for the <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes Vikings</a> and with the <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale Sharks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> Rugby is increasing in popularity, especially with the annual Safari Sevens tournament. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_rugby_sevens_team" title="Kenya national rugby sevens team">Kenya Sevens team</a> ranked 9th in the IRB Sevens World Series for the 2006 season. In 2016, the team beat Fiji at the Singapore Sevens finals, making Kenya the second African nation after South Africa to win a World Series championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> was once also a regional powerhouse in football. However, its dominance has been eroded by wrangles within the now defunct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenya_Football_Federation" title="Kenya Football Federation">Kenya Football Federation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> leading to a suspension by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> which was lifted in March 2007.
</p><p>In the motor rallying arena, Kenya is home to the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Safari_Rally" title="Safari Rally">Safari Rally</a>, commonly acknowledged as one of the toughest rallies in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> First held in 1953, it was a part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> for many years until its exclusion after the 2002 event owing to financial difficulties. Some of the best rally drivers in the world have taken part in and won the rally, such as <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Björn Waldegård">Björn Waldegård</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommi_M%C3%A4kinen" title="Tommi Mäkinen">Tommi Mäkinen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shekhar_Mehta" title="Shekhar Mehta">Shekhar Mehta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz_Sr." title="Carlos Sainz Sr.">Carlos Sainz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae" title="Colin McRae">Colin McRae</a>. The Safari Rally returned to the world championship in <a href="/wiki/2021_Safari_Rally" title="2021 Safari Rally">2021</a>, after the 2003-2019 events ran as part of the <a href="/wiki/African_Rally_Championship" title="African Rally Championship">African Rally Championship</a>.
</p><p>Nairobi has hosted several major continental sports events, including the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_1993" title="FIBA Africa Championship 1993">FIBA Africa Championship 1993</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenya_national_basketball_team" title="Kenya national basketball team">Kenya's national basketball team</a> finished in the top four, its best performance to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kenya also has its own <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team, the Kenya Ice Lions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> The team's home ground is the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Ice_Rink" title="Solar Ice Rink">Solar Ice Rink</a> at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Panari_Sky_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Panari Sky Centre (page does not exist)">Panari Sky Centre</a> in Nairobi,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> which is the first and largest <a href="/wiki/Ice_rink" title="Ice rink">ice rink</a> in all of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="576" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/220px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/330px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/440px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukuma_wiki" title="Sukuma wiki">sukuma wiki</a>, staples of Kenyan cuisine</div></div></div>
<p>Kenyans generally have three meals in a day—breakfast (<i>kiamsha kinywa</i>), lunch (<i>chakula cha mchana</i>), and supper (<i>chakula cha jioni</i> or simply <i>chajio</i>). In between, they have the 10-o'clock tea (<i>chai ya saa nne</i>) and 4 p.m. tea (<i>chai ya saa kumi</i>). Breakfast is usually tea or porridge with bread, <a href="/wiki/Chapati" title="Chapati">chapati</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahamri" title="Mahamri">mahamri</a>, boiled sweet potatoes, or <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>. <a href="/wiki/Githeri" title="Githeri">Githeri</a> is a common lunchtime dish in many households, while <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> with vegetables, sour milk (<a href="/wiki/Mursik" title="Mursik">mursik</a>), meat, fish, or any other stew is generally eaten by much of the population for lunch or supper. Regional variations and dishes also exist.
</p><p>In western Kenya, among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luo_(Kenya_and_Tanzania)" title="Luo (Kenya and Tanzania)">Luo</a>, fish is a common dish; among the <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a>, who dominate much of the Rift Valley Region, mursik—sour milk—is a common drink.
</p><p>In cities such as Nairobi, there are fast-food restaurants, including <a href="/wiki/Steers" title="Steers">Steers</a>, <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> There are also many fish-and-chips shops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cheese_in_Kenya" title="Cheese in Kenya">Cheese</a> is becoming more popular in Kenya, with consumption increasing particularly among the middle class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>
</p>
